<div id="review_26947849" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26947849" />
    <a title="Jake" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/972904-jake"><img alt="Jake" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1230756051p2/972904.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26947849?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jake" href="/user/show/972904-jake">Jake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/972904-jake?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/972904-jake?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/972904-jake?shelf=favorite-titles">favorite-titles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/972904-jake?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/972904-jake?shelf=pulp">pulp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/972904-jake?shelf=sword-and-scorcery">sword-and-scorcery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/972904-jake?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26947849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1323473989252722341">The Bloody Crown of Conan is the third in a series of five collections of REH’s work being published by Del Rey. Three of those volumes feature Howard’s original, unedited Conan stories. The other two cover different fantasy heroes of Howard’s, namely Bran Mak Morn and Solomon Kane (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.livejournal.com/users/j_stone_/2005/05/03/'>http://www.livejournal.com/users/j_st...</a>). Apparently, I never reviewed the first Conan collection, the Coming of Conan the Cimmerian, but I liked it. And guess what. I liked this too.<br/><br/>Bloody Crown of Conan contains o</span>
  <span id="freeText1323473989252722341" style="display:none">The Bloody Crown of Conan is the third in a series of five collections of REH’s work being published by Del Rey. Three of those volumes feature Howard’s original, unedited Conan stories. The other two cover different fantasy heroes of Howard’s, namely Bran Mak Morn and Solomon Kane (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.livejournal.com/users/j_stone_/2005/05/03/">http://www.livejournal.com/users/j_st...</a>). Apparently, I never reviewed the first Conan collection, the Coming of Conan the Cimmerian, but I liked it. And guess what. I liked this too.<br /><br />Bloody Crown of Conan contains only three stories: “People of the Black Circle,” “The Hour of the Dragon,” and “A Witch is Born.” While it may not sound like much, “The Hour of the Dragon” is the only full length Conan novel that Howard ever wrote. It’s a very neat story, set during the time when Conan is king of Aquilonia. In short, Conan is disposed by an evil necromancer and the mortals he conspires with, and must go on a quest to retrieve something that can kill the necromancer and allow him to reclaim the throne. Lots of high adventure, sword-fighting, strange, otherworldly horrors, and no small amount of intrigue. The other two stories are shorter (obviously), but still packed with good stuff.<br /><br />I really enjoy Howard’s writing style. It’s very straightforward, but evocative at the same time. He does get into some purple prose on occasion, but it’s the sort of purple prose that’s fun to read. My only real complaint would be that he sometimes over-uses certain descriptors, particularly those involving wolves and panthers. Still, he treads a line between cliché and epic epithet enough that it only rarely bothers me. Oh, and occasionally he starts to drift into the Lovecraft “it was so horrible, I cannot describe it, except in horribly vague terms” trap, which is kind of annoying, especially because Howard’s descriptions of everything else are wonderful. Conan’s crucifixition in “A Witch is Born” had me shuddering on the T. Powerful stuff.<br /><br />Yes, Conan does get crucified. One of the interesting things about reading these stories is seeing where the Schwarzanegger movie cribbed certain scenes or ideas to create the story it did. In the end, the Schwarzanegger Conan is substantively different from the actual Conan, but I still love the movie, and think it’s very well done. Of course, I’m an unrepentant Schwarzanegger fan for a variety of reasons, so take that for what you will.<br /><br />Bloody Crown of Conan, and indeed, all the Conan stories, really are required reading for fantasy fans. There’s a good reason why the character has survived this long…he’s awesome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1323473989252722341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9368931186679496975">Two of these are novellas, and The Hour of the Dragon can be construed as a complete book, the only book Howard wrote for Conan the Cimmerian. See my review of The Coming of Conan the Cimmerian for Dale Rippke's ordering.<br/><br/>A Witch Shall be Born: This novella deals with themes of paranoia, twist plots and extreme irony, sometimes the cruel type. A queen discovers her evil twin, a witch, has survived being left in the desert to die. Queen Tauramis is arrested and thrown in the dungeon, where it's up</span>
  <span id="freeText9368931186679496975" style="display:none">Two of these are novellas, and The Hour of the Dragon can be construed as a complete book, the only book Howard wrote for Conan the Cimmerian. See my review of The Coming of Conan the Cimmerian for Dale Rippke's ordering.<br /><br />A Witch Shall be Born: This novella deals with themes of paranoia, twist plots and extreme irony, sometimes the cruel type. A queen discovers her evil twin, a witch, has survived being left in the desert to die. Queen Tauramis is arrested and thrown in the dungeon, where it's up to defiant Conan, captain of the queen's guard, to save her. 5/5<br /><br />The People of the Black Circle: Another king's-sister (king is killed, she vows revenge), Queen Yasmina is kidnapped by Conan and held hostage in exchange for seven of his men. They were kidnapped by HER to try to force him to kill the Black Seers of Yimsha. Kerim Shah, the man who killed the king, is leading an army through the mountain pass during the turmoil, and Conan is going to need all the allies he can get. 3/5<br /><br />The Hour of the Dragon: Conan is around 45. Continuity in the plot of The Scarlet Citadel is seen as it returns to the problem of Numidedes being slain by Conan, and his heir Valerius returning to the storyline. Desiring the throne, Valerius and his men resurrect Xaltotun, an evil 3,000 year old sorcerer, doubling back on an earlier plotline from a short story. Conan is defeated in battle and captured, but then freed by a slave-girl, Zenobia. The only thing that can defeat the evil Xaltotun is the exact same object that resurrected him - the Heart of Ahriman. His journey takes him through all the lands of Hyboria, Conan promises to return for the beautiful slave, whom he vows to make his queen. 5/5</span>

<div id="review_496252908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/496252908" />
    <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas"><img alt="Benjamin Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451660582p2/4209082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/496252908?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Thomas" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas">Benjamin Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=anthologies-short-stories">anthologies-short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=fantasy-sword-sorcery">fantasy-sword-sorcery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=pulp-old-and-new">pulp-old-and-new</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer496252908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13115614810593210675">This book compiles three of Robert E. Howard's longer Conan works, including the only full length Conan novel that he ever wrote, "The Hour of the Dragon." It also contains "The People of the Black Circle" as well as "A Witch Shall Be Born" which contains probably the most famous scene in all of Conan literature: the one where he gets nailed to a tree, crucified really, and left to the mercy of the hungry vultures and the elements. As the title implies, all three stories are from Conan's later d</span>
  <span id="freeText13115614810593210675" style="display:none">This book compiles three of Robert E. Howard's longer Conan works, including the only full length Conan novel that he ever wrote, "The Hour of the Dragon." It also contains "The People of the Black Circle" as well as "A Witch Shall Be Born" which contains probably the most famous scene in all of Conan literature: the one where he gets nailed to a tree, crucified really, and left to the mercy of the hungry vultures and the elements. As the title implies, all three stories are from Conan's later days, when he is king. <br /><br />As in all of these Del Rey editions of Howard's work, the book also contains several untitled synopsis (synopses? synopsizes?), fragments, etc. as well as a thought-provoking essay on Howard and his life and times as it pertains to the included stories.<br /><br />I think the noble nature of Conan really comes out in these stories, particularly in "The Hour of the Dragon". When Conan has the opportunity to conquer a neighboring kingdom he says, "Let others dream imperial dreams. I but wish to hold what is mine. I have no desire to rule an empire welded together by blood and fire. It's one thing to seize a throne with the aid of its subjects and rule them with their consent. It's another to subjugate a foreign realm and rule it by fear." As Patrice Louinet says in the essay, "Whoever had the idea of retitling Howard's novel, 'Conan the Conqueror' had evidently not understood its theme: Conan is anything but a conqueror by nature."<br /><br />Enjoyable reading and, of course, absolutely required reading for Conan enthusiasts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13115614810593210675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1983325551" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1983325551" />
    <a title="Craig" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83180-craig"><img alt="Craig" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544792260p2/83180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1983325551?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Craig" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Craig" href="/user/show/83180-craig">Craig</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781400162246" href="/book/show/7124308-the-bloody-crown-of-conan">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1983325551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12458133933009727797">I listened to the 15-disc audio version of this collection; I've read the stories several times over the years in various formats. There are three stories in the collection, three of the longer ones that Howard produced; The People of the Black Circle, A Witch Shall Be Born, and The Hour of the Dragon. The stories are performed well, and it was interesting to compare Conan's character as a king and as a bandit and adventurer from one to the next. The Hour of the Dragon (which I remember as Conan</span>
  <span id="freeText12458133933009727797" style="display:none">I listened to the 15-disc audio version of this collection; I've read the stories several times over the years in various formats. There are three stories in the collection, three of the longer ones that Howard produced; The People of the Black Circle, A Witch Shall Be Born, and The Hour of the Dragon. The stories are performed well, and it was interesting to compare Conan's character as a king and as a bandit and adventurer from one to the next. The Hour of the Dragon (which I remember as Conan the Conqueror; I read my Dad's Gnome Press edition back before the Hyborian Age ended!) was the only novel-length Conan story that Howard wrote and I think it's the best of these three. It's also interesting to note how many of the little bits and pieces that Howard mentioned were picked up and recycled by the various writers who continued the Conan adventures over the years. This edition also includes a number of unfinished fragments by Howard and some lengthy non-fiction discussions by other authors that didn't suit me as well in an audio version. I would have preferred to skim them and possibly skip over some of the questionably scholarly analyses. I enjoyed revisiting the three main stories very much, though. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12458133933009727797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7402367070773227291">I guess I'm a confirmed Howard fan-boy at this point, since I can't get enough of his stuff. Here was no exception, since "People of the Black Circle" and "Hour of the Dragon" are among his better stories. "A Witch Shall be Born" is less strong, but it does have the crucifixion scene, so that counts for something.<br/><br/>Some of these stories I already own in other collections, but I picked this book up new at Barnes & Noble as part of my personal crusade to preserve physical bookstores. <br/><br/>It was a nice t</span>
  <span id="freeText7402367070773227291" style="display:none">I guess I'm a confirmed Howard fan-boy at this point, since I can't get enough of his stuff. Here was no exception, since "People of the Black Circle" and "Hour of the Dragon" are among his better stories. "A Witch Shall be Born" is less strong, but it does have the crucifixion scene, so that counts for something.<br /><br />Some of these stories I already own in other collections, but I picked this book up new at Barnes &amp; Noble as part of my personal crusade to preserve physical bookstores. <br /><br />It was a nice tidbit seeing Howard's outlines and the "Untitled Draft", which I'd read earlier as completed by L. Sprague de Camp. <br /><br />Anyhow, this is the real stuff. Sword and sorcery should be like this, not stuffy and quaint like Tolkien or slow and bogged down in politics like Martin or Goodkind. And while I'm on the subject, Robert Jordan was no damn good at writing Conan, those books were like a paint-by-numbers TV version of the character. Accept no substitutes. Read Howard! </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10385157025445004242">Where as the stories in The Coming of Conan the Cimmerian were short and sweet, the novellas combined in The Bloody Crown of Conan are enjoyable because you get to spend a lot more time getting into the mind of Conan the Barbarian. <br/><br/>You can feel his paranoia and understandable apprehension behind his hyper-macho exterior.   <span id="freeText10385157025445004242" style="display:none">Where as the stories in The Coming of Conan the Cimmerian were short and sweet, the novellas combined in The Bloody Crown of Conan are enjoyable because you get to spend a lot more time getting into the mind of Conan the Barbarian. <br /><br />You can feel his paranoia and understandable apprehension behind his hyper-macho exterior. It was also refreshing to realize that while he is brutal, he is not an incompetent brute. This was something that I feel the film adaptations did not capture very well.<br /><br />It is also fun to read some of Howard's story synopses for other stories that never got published. There was all sorts of potential for sure, and it's too bad Robert committed suicide very likely due to mental health issues. One could only wonder what else could have come from Howard's imagination had he continued writing stories.<br /><br /> If you have never picked up a Conan book before, I would start with this. The stories are very good. So good you will only want more of it! I know I do.</span>

<div id="review_1845799373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1845799373" />
    <a title="Earl P. Dean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50437060-earl-p-dean"><img alt="Earl P. Dean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451097606p2/50437060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1845799373?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Earl P. Dean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Earl P. Dean" href="/user/show/50437060-earl-p-dean">Earl P. Dean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1845799373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13818209107632223262">This was a good Robert E. Howard Conan story. It exhibited a more refined style of writing that showed Howard's growth as a writer, and that was good. But I did notice it seemed a little more considered, and that might have taken something away from the savagery, the off the cuff, gut reaction writing I'm used to seeing from REH; until this, I'd never had the feeling that he was ever second guessing his effort. Overall, the story was well written, had lots of bloody battles and dark sorceries, a</span>
  <span id="freeText13818209107632223262" style="display:none">This was a good Robert E. Howard Conan story. It exhibited a more refined style of writing that showed Howard's growth as a writer, and that was good. But I did notice it seemed a little more considered, and that might have taken something away from the savagery, the off the cuff, gut reaction writing I'm used to seeing from REH; until this, I'd never had the feeling that he was ever second guessing his effort. Overall, the story was well written, had lots of bloody battles and dark sorceries, and ended well. While Xaltotun was probably the most powerful adversary that Conan had ever faced, he was offstage for a lot of the story. I can see why, because if he'd been up front and center and facing Conan regularly, the story would have simply ended. As much as I like Conan as a fighter, he'd have had little to no chance most of the time.</span>

    <a title="Damien Sulla-Menashe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49498278-damien-sulla-menashe"><img alt="Damien Sulla-Menashe" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1589849987?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Damien Sulla-Menashe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Damien Sulla-Menashe" href="/user/show/49498278-damien-sulla-menashe">Damien Sulla-Menashe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1589849987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10131208545480465378">The great part of this Conan anthology is that the stories are presented in the order that Howard wrote them instead of some internal chronology. Because of this the reader can see the evolution of his most used phrases and plots. While the stories have many similar themes and characters, the action is exciting and his descriptions of people and places get more elaborate which pulls you in more. This second book contains three of his longest stories. I enjoyed the more complex plots, especially </span>
  <span id="freeText10131208545480465378" style="display:none">The great part of this Conan anthology is that the stories are presented in the order that Howard wrote them instead of some internal chronology. Because of this the reader can see the evolution of his most used phrases and plots. While the stories have many similar themes and characters, the action is exciting and his descriptions of people and places get more elaborate which pulls you in more. This second book contains three of his longest stories. I enjoyed the more complex plots, especially the second story called Hour of the Dragon, because they show other sides of the protagonist beyond the simple barbarian. However, the shorter stories are end to end excitement without any sort of pause and it seems like that's the core of what makes these stories so great.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10131208545480465378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7572126-stephen-richter?shelf=dead-tree">dead-tree</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7572126-stephen-richter?shelf=s-l-short-stories-challenge">s-l-short-stories-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7572126-stephen-richter?shelf=sword-challenge-2019">sword-challenge-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7572126-stephen-richter?shelf=anthologies">anthologies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2758538939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13830523451409142349">A few short stories and the only novel of Conan. I kind of have the feeling if you have read one Conan you have read then all. There were a few problematic paragraphs, but as it was written in 1930s it was not out of the ordinary. I was kind of surprised not to find more. I have the other 2 volumes of the series and will return if I have the time in the coming years.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_585224961" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/585224961" />
    <a title="Brian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11717318-brian"><img alt="Brian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590770967p2/11717318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/585224961?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian" href="/user/show/11717318-brian">Brian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11717318-brian?shelf=conan">conan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11717318-brian?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11717318-brian?shelf=weird-fiction">weird-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11717318-brian?shelf=sword-and-sorcery">sword-and-sorcery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer585224961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6373834076981498282">I admit I was a bit worried when I first started reading this book, because it's a truism that writers who are excellent at short stories tend to be unable to maintain their pacing when they try their hand at the longer form--see also <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/23001.Fritz_Leiber' title='Fritz Leiber' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fritz Leiber</a>. Then again, I suppose I shouldn't have worried, since the first Conan story I read years ago was a novel form of "The Hour of the Dragon" and that's what got me interested in reading more <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/66700.Robert_E__Howard' title='Robert E. Howard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Howard</a> stories in the first place.<br/><br/>There are a few things I noti</span>
  <span id="freeText6373834076981498282" style="display:none">I admit I was a bit worried when I first started reading this book, because it's a truism that writers who are excellent at short stories tend to be unable to maintain their pacing when they try their hand at the longer form--see also <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/23001.Fritz_Leiber" title="Fritz Leiber" rel="nofollow noopener">Fritz Leiber</a>. Then again, I suppose I shouldn't have worried, since the first Conan story I read years ago was a novel form of "The Hour of the Dragon" and that's what got me interested in reading more <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/66700.Robert_E__Howard" title="Robert E. Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Howard</a> stories in the first place.<br /><br />There are a few things I noticed as I read through the three stories contained herein. The first is that in "The People of the Black Circle," there's even less effort to disguise the various places and countries Howard describes than there has been previously. Aquilonia immediately evokes the Roman Empire (c.f. <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aquila_(Roman)" rel="nofollow noopener">Aquila</a>, or the Roman city of <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lacedonia" rel="nofollow noopener">Aquilonia</a>), but many of the names are also Greek, and some are neither: Tanasul, for example. While Stygia is pretty transparently Egypt-but-evil-plus-snakes, Brythunia, Hyperborea, Zamora, and so on aren't so easily mappable on to currently-existing areas of the world.<br /><br />Not so in the east, where Iranistan, Vendhya, Afghulistan, the Himelian Mountains, and so on are all just the historic places we know with the names scratched out and written over. This is called out in the introduction as a good aspect of Howard's work, since it allows the reader to immediately identify where the story is taking place and pull in the relevant cultural associations without Howard needing to waste time explaining anything about the setting. I can see that point of view, but at the same time, I like the Hyborian stories better when they seem more fantastical. Figuring out that Cimmerians are just Celtic people and Crom comes from <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crom_Cruach" rel="nofollow noopener">Crom Cruach</a> did active harm to my enjoyment of the Conan stories, though obviously not enough to prevent me from reading more. When I see "Iranistan," I just think Howard should have tried a bit harder.<br /><br />The sorcery in these stories is also much more on the side of mystical gestures than weird science. It seems to move from story to story, and sometimes it seems more like pre-scientific chemistry or physics, but sometimes it's tearing people's hearts out with telekinesis or raising the dead, and these stories fall into the latter category.<br /><br />The longest story in the book, and definitely the standout, is "The Hour of the Dragon." The basic plot is similar to "The Phoenix on the Sword," where a group of conspirators utilize a wizard's aid to fight against Conan, but this time Conan actually loses and has to go through a lot of difficulties--or enemies' skulls, I could say--to get his throne back, including a trip to Stygia. It is admittedly all a bit similar, in that there's nothing in this story that makes it stand out from other Conan stories other than its length, but that's not as much of a condemnation as it appears. As I said earlier, Howard's quality doesn't decline even in the longer form, so "The Hour of the Dragon" is never a chore to read and it certainly doesn't drag, but it doesn't have anything to propel it to a higher level. There's just more of it.<br /><br />Well, okay, Xaltotun is the best Conan villain I've run into so far. And even though the scene with Akivasha comes out of nowhere and could be cut with no loss to the story, I like that it's in there. "I am Akivasha! I am the woman who never died, who never grew old!" is potent phrasing.<br /><br />It did bring home an interesting principle, though. Conan has incredibly charisma and personal magnetism, and he's constantly shown being thrown into situations among just about every people or culture that exists in Hyboria and rising up to command, but that's all he has to rely on. As soon as he apparently dies in the first battle against the Nemedians, Aquilonia goes to hell. The barons all start fighting each other, people clamor for a king--any king--to keep them safe, and no one really gives any thought to trying to keep Conan's united, peaceful Aquilonia alive other than a few border lords. But as soon as he returns, everyone flocks to his banner and crushes his enemies. I'm not sure if Howard had a greater message when he wrote Conan this way, but it seems to me to be one of the disadvantages of the seemingly Übermenschen barbarians in Howard's world. Personal loyalty is powerful, but societal stability comes from loyalty to institutions and the rule of law, which Conan doesn't and cannot encourage. There's a kind of tragedy to Conan's life, then, where he's always being cast down, builds himself a ladder to get back to the heights, then is cast down again, but while he can do it, there's nothing permanent about it. It's a ladder, not a staircase, and it won't last long after him.<br /><br />"The People of the Black Circle" has the problems I mentioned earlier about being almost too familiar, but if that doesn't bother you as much as it bothered me it's the second-best story in the book. It also absolutely brings the sorcery part of "swords and sorcery," since the previously-mentioned Black Circle is a group of sorcerers, but since it's neither as good as "The Hour of the Dragon" nor as tepid as "A Witch Shall Be Born," I don't have much to say about it. It does serve as a counterpoint to Conan's easy ability to insinuate himself into any group he's in, though perhaps it's because he's also among barbarians. If the hill tribes count as barbarians--I'm pretty sure the only people I've heard of described as barbarian in the Conan stories have been the Cimmerians.<br /><br />"A Witch Shall Be Born" was...okay. I didn't find it that interesting, maybe because Conan only comes in at the end and the beginning, but maybe also because of a point made in the epilogue of the book. There's a scene where Conan is crucified, hangs on the cross for hours, fights off vultures, then has the cross chopped down, the nails ripped out, and has to walk to a horse, get on, and ride ten miles to his rescuer's camp. And he does, and survives, and apparently suffers no ill effects. That starts crossing into ridiculousness to me. I mean, in Howard's world, being a barbarian makes you a superhero already and there's a lot you have to accept about how growing up in tents on a lonely moor makes one an invincible warrior who can fight ten people with one hand tied behind their back, but surviving crucifixion apparently unharmed is a bit much. And the rest of the story is relatively prosaic, so it doesn't serve to overcome that...hesitation to engage, I'll call it.<br /><br />So, the bookends are adequate, but "The Hour of the Dragon" pulls <i>The Bloody Crown of Conan</i> up to four stars for me. One book to go, and if it can merely maintain the quality that Howard has exhibited until this point, it will have been time more than well-spent.<br /><br />Previous review: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/585224620" rel="nofollow noopener">The Coming of Conan the Cimmerian</a>.<br />Next review: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/585225160" rel="nofollow noopener">The Conquering Sword of Conan</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6373834076981498282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3422085875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3422085875" />
    <a title="Dave" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82298-dave"><img alt="Dave" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574887884p2/82298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3422085875?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dave" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dave" href="/user/show/82298-dave">Dave</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3422085875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12706543955687885289"> Three of the longer Conan stories by REH along with drafts, notes, and synopsis' are in this book.<br/>"The People of the Black Circle" involves Conan, now chief of the Afghuli tribe, kidnapping Princess Yasmina in an effort to buy back seven of his captured men while eventually pitted against the sorcery of the Black Seers. An interesting character in Khemsa is written by Howard as a love stricken underling wizard to the Seers who eventually helps Conan out with the Black Seers.<br/> In "Hour of the Dra</span>
  <span id="freeText12706543955687885289" style="display:none"> Three of the longer Conan stories by REH along with drafts, notes, and synopsis' are in this book.<br />"The People of the Black Circle" involves Conan, now chief of the Afghuli tribe, kidnapping Princess Yasmina in an effort to buy back seven of his captured men while eventually pitted against the sorcery of the Black Seers. An interesting character in Khemsa is written by Howard as a love stricken underling wizard to the Seers who eventually helps Conan out with the Black Seers.<br /> In "Hour of the Dragon" we get Howard's first Conan novel which is a sprawling tale of King Conan and his loss of the crown to a cabal of usurpers who resurrect a long dead sorcerer in an effort to remove Conan and extend political influence in and around the region of Aquilonia. A true masterpiece by Howard and a story that takes Conan all over Hyboria from Argos to Stygia and all points elsewhere.<br /> Last is "A Witch Shall Be Born" which is most famous for the crucifiction of Conan. Queen Taramis of Khauran is imprisoned by her evil twin Salome who than impersonates the queen and rules with chaos and terror along with the brutal Kothian Constantius. Conan overcomes and a thrilling ending to the story occurs in which Conan seems more of a bit player to the uprising of the people and the soldiers who help take down the proverbial monster this time in the form of Thaug, a large frog-like beast. <br /> Three major tales in the Conan myth well worth the read. Again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12706543955687885289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7jhlsbGrFnbkI+IMdzxfhIVgdsps9mRVWUluVJwZz4eGsDKRvWOaa/7W3qP81/+Y0ULqvLzo+BuHD+L8oA/teA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2FywYclHWymPjtJpAh2YxMvNws07yq7duu+pRm3E6gGw1OdBxY/XNJV77saJ9jjYn+9eu+vUMpNkqSXuUdLI/g==')})
  }

Author Michael Moorcock, already a major player in science fiction, cemented his position in the fantasy pantheon with the five-book Elric saga, of which Elric of Melniboné is the first installment. The book\'s namesake, the brooding albino emperor of the dying nation of Melniboné, is a sort of Superman for Goths, truly an archetype of the genre.\n\nThe youthful Elric is a cynical and melancholy king, heir to a nation whose 100,000-year rule of the world ended less than 500 years hence. More interested in brooding contemplation than holding the throne, Elric is a reluctant ruler, but he also realizes that no other worthy successor exists and the survival of his once-powerful, decadent nation depends on him alone. Elric\'s nefarious, brutish cousin Yrkoon has no patience for his physically weak kinsman, and he plots constantly to seize Elric\'s throne, usually over his dead body. Elric of Melniboné follows Yrkoon\'s scheming, reaching its climax in a battle between Elric and Yrkoon with the demonic runeblades Stormbringer and Mournblade. In this battle, Elric gains control of the soul-stealing Stormbringer, an event that proves pivotal to the Elric saga. --Paul Hughes<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"16319563176774875767\" href=\"#\" <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7365441665641203697">Robert Ervin Howard was an American pulp writer of fantasy, horror, historical adventure, boxing, western, and detective fiction. Howard wrote "over three-hundred stories and seven-hundred poems of raw power and unbridled emotion" and is especially noted for his memorable depictions of "a sombre universe of swashbuckling adventure and darkling horror."<br/><br/>He is well known for having created — in the p</span>
  <span id="freeText7365441665641203697" style="display:none">Robert Ervin Howard was an American pulp writer of fantasy, horror, historical adventure, boxing, western, and detective fiction. Howard wrote "over three-hundred stories and seven-hundred poems of raw power and unbridled emotion" and is especially noted for his memorable depictions of "a sombre universe of swashbuckling adventure and darkling horror."<br /><br />He is well known for having created — in the pages of the legendary Depression-era pulp magazine Weird Tales — the character Conan the Cimmerian, a.k.a. Conan the Barbarian, a literary icon whose pop-culture imprint can only be compared to such icons as Tarzan of the Apes, Count Dracula, Sherlock Holmes, and James Bond.<br /><br />-Wikipedia<br /><br /><i><b>Librarian Note:</b> There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /></span>
